Bedrock credentials are set, then the backend has to initialize the client

‚Źļ I've now thoroughly mapped both the backend event system and the existing UI.
  Here's what I found, then a few decisions I need from you before writing the
  spec.

  What I verified

  Backend event emission (src/ailf/core/events/)
  - The changepoint pipeline emits a typed, ordered stream of StageEvents
  (frozen dataclass: run_id, seq, ts, stage, status, payload) to sinks. There
  are 11 stages in causal order: config_resolved ‚Üí split_built ‚Üí 
  changepoint_detection ‚Üí baseline_full_history_prophet ‚Üí 
  baseline_naive_workflow ‚Üí diagnostics_computed ‚Üí visual_inspection ‚Üí 
  decision_iteration (√óN) ‚Üí validation_outcome (√óN) ‚Üí final_evaluation ‚Üí 
  run_complete.
  - Payloads are rich enough for everything you want: decision_iteration carries
  the agent's chosen tool, params, rationale, and expected_effect;
  final_evaluation carries test_metrics_by_method (MAE/RMSE/WAPE/sMAPE for
  full-history Prophet, naive, and agent); run_complete carries the winner. The
  final graph data (3 forecast series + actuals + train/val/test boundaries +
  changepoint markers) is all available. So yes ‚ÄĒ an interactive Plotly graph
  with a verdict banner is entirely feasible.

  One important reality about "live": the prelude stages (config ‚Üí diagnostics)
  are emitted one-by-one as they happen, but the agent reasoning loop
  (decision/validation iterations, visual inspection, final eval) is currently
  emitted in a single burst after the LangGraph run finishes
  (pipeline.py:264-275). So out of the box, the most interesting part ‚ÄĒ the
  agent thinking iteration-by-iteration ‚ÄĒ would appear all at once at the end,
  not live. This is the crux decision below.

  Dataset contract ‚ÄĒ your assumption is correct. Required columns are exactly ds
  (datetime) and y (numeric), hardcoded (datasets.py:41, pipeline.py:119-120).
  Scenario splits come from pocs/changepoint/data/scenario_metadata.json
  (train_end / validation_horizon / test_horizon). Custom CSV uses ratio-based
  splitting.

  Model init ‚ÄĒ one discrepancy with your ask. The provider auto-detect
  (resolve.py:49-60) currently checks AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID first, then 
  ANTHROPIC_API_KEY ‚ÄĒ the reverse of what you described. You want
  Anthropic-API-first, Bedrock-fallback. I'll flip this priority (it's a clear
  requirement, not a guess). The "Sonnet 4.6 / Opus 4.8" friendly names will map
  to the right ID per provider in the backend, reusing the existing
  _BEDROCK_TO_ANTHROPIC_MODEL_ID table.

  UI pathways ‚ÄĒ you're right, there are ~3. All by Sowmya: (1) the big Streamlit
  app (drift/streamlit_app.py) which itself bundles a drift-detect path with
  Qwen/Ollama/Claude, a Prophet fallback, and a call into the changepoint
  run_scenario; (2) a FastAPI-served embedded HTML/Plotly UI
  (drift/pipeline.py); (3) the Plotly utilities. Your described control pane (13
  diagnostics, 6 tools, scenario metadata, visual + reasoning models,
  train/val/test) maps cleanly and exclusively onto the changepoint pipeline.

  Now the decisions:

‚Źļ Dynamic workflow "Verify exactly how the UI and agent core are (de)coupled from the changepoint/drift/anomaly pathways" completed ¬∑ 2m 51s

‚Źļ I dug into this precisely, and your instinct is half right ‚ÄĒ right about the
  agent, wrong about the symmetry of the "pathways." Here's the real picture.

  Your mental model is correct ‚ÄĒ about the agent core

  The ReAct loop genuinely is pathway-independent. src/ailf/core/agent/ (engine,
  nodes, registry, runtime) imports zero changepoint/drift/anomaly symbols. The
  core only speaks duck-typed contracts: a pipeline hands it a RunContext
  carrying a tool registry, a diagnostics bundle, prompts, a data split, and
  models ‚ÄĒ and the loop runs identically regardless of use case. There's exactly
  one intentional, documented exception: final_evaluation_node (nodes.py:129)
  has a local import of changepoint.baselines to compute the test-fold
  baselines. That's the only core‚Üípipeline coupling, and it's flagged as "keeps
  core import-clean of pipeline."

  So: core = generic agent loop + registry + events + backtest + metrics. 
  Pipeline = supplies tools + diagnostics + prompts + dataset. That part is
  exactly as you thought.

  But the "three pathways" are not three peer agent pipelines

  This is the part that doesn't match your model:

  Dir: changepoint/
  What it actually is: ‚úÖ The only real agent pipeline. run_scenario() wires
    tools/diagnostics/prompts into build_agent_graph() and runs the core loop.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Dir: drift/
  What it actually is: ‚ĚĆ Not an agent pipeline at all. It's a FastAPI service +

    the Streamlit UI + standalone non-agent demos (llm_reason.py =
    Qwen/CUSUM/Claude detector, fallback.py = a hand-rolled LLM-picks-a-tool +
    Prophet routine). It has zero imports of build_agent_graph/RunContext. It
    reaches into changepoint via a lazy import run_scenario.
  ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
  Dir: anomaly/
  What it actually is: ‚ĚĆ A deterministic scripted diagnostic. No agent loop, no

    event emission.

  So where is the coupling you're feeling? In the UI, not the agent.

  The reason a consumer is exposed to "drift/changepoint/anomaly" is purely an
  artifact of where the UI was built and what it bundles:

  1. The UI physically lives inside pipelines/drift/streamlit_app.py ‚ÄĒ so it
  inherited the drift vocabulary and a dependency on drift-only modules
  (llm_reason, fallback).
  2. It offers three invocation paths, only one of which is the real agent: a
  "Bedrock Changepoint Pipeline" toggle that calls run_scenario; a standalone
  "detect & forecast" path (Qwen/Ollama/CUSUM); and a FastAPI fallback. The
  other two are demo scaffolding.
  3. It doesn't even consume the rich event stream. This corrects something I
  said earlier: the current UI reconstructs progress by polling the thread and 
  reading artifacts off disk after the run finishes (metrics.json,
  forecast_comparison.csv). It never reads events.jsonl / the EventEmitter. So
  the "live streaming of events" you want is genuinely a new capability, not a
  cleanup of existing wiring.

  One more nuance worth knowing: the event taxonomy itself
  (core/events/stages.py) has changepoint-flavored stage names baked into a
  closed enum (changepoint_detection, baseline_full_history_prophet, ‚Ä¶). The
  envelope (stage + status + payload) is fully generic and a UI can render any
  event polymorphically ‚ÄĒ but the stage names lean changepoint. Since we only
  run changepoint, that's harmless; I just want you to know it's not a perfectly
  use-case-neutral bus.

  What "streamlining" therefore means concretely

  A single clean UI that:
  - Lives in a neutral location (e.g. src/ailf/ui/ or app/), not inside
  pipelines/drift/, so consumers never see pathway vocabulary.
  - Depends only on the changepoint agent's run_scenario + ConfigOverride + the
  scenario metadata + the generic event stream. ~5 backend symbols instead of
  ~15.
  - Drops entirely: llm_reason.detect/detect_streaming, the CUSUM fallback,
  fallback.run_fallback_pipeline, the Qwen/Ollama controls, the FastAPI HTML UI,
  and the duplicate visual-inspection code.
  - Consumes the event stream live (the genuinely new piece), then renders the
  final interactive Plotly verdict graph.

  Given all that, here are the real decisions left ‚ÄĒ and they're cleaner now
  that we know only changepoint is real:

  What the spec captures (grounded in verified code facts):
  - One streamlined interface in a neutral src/ailf/ui/ ‚ÄĒ left control pane
  (Start, scenario-or-CSV dataset, visual + reasoning model selectors,
  13-diagnostic toggles, tool toggles, visual on/off) and right area (run

  provider order). Per Principle VII and the per-change gates, those edits are
  review-gated and must keep core tests green ‚ÄĒ the spec encodes that as a hard
  requirement.

          +`app.py` is the thin Streamlit shell, and `run_controller.py` 
          +is the only place that touches threads. Backend edits are surg
          +ically confined to the four files named above.

      117 +1. **Live emission via `.stream()` from the driver, NOT inside
          + node bodies.** LangGraph `1.2.4` `StateGraph.invoke()` runs t
          +he `visual ‚ą• diagnostics` fan-out serially in one thread; emit
          +ting inside nodes would reintroduce the causal-ordering jitter
          + the existing design deliberately avoids. Instead, the pipelin
          +e driver iterates `app.stream(...)` and emits each stage as it
          +s node completes ‚ÄĒ keeping `seq` assignment single-threaded an
          +d monotonic. The current post-invoke reconstruction block (`pi
          +peline.py:264-275`) is **removed** to avoid double emission (w
          +hich would break `test_event_stream.py`'s strict-monotonic + c
          +ausal-order asserts).                                         
      118  
       99 -ios/ or android/                                              
      100 -‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ [platform-specific structure: feature modules, UI flows, p
          -latform tests]                                                
      101 -```                                                           
      119 +2. **Generic `QueueEventSink` + `extra_sinks` injection.** `Ev
          +entEmitter` already fans out to a `list[EventSink]`. Add a `Qu
          +eueEventSink(queue.Queue)` implementing `write(event)` ‚Üí `queu
          +e.put(event.to_dict())`, and add `extra_sinks: list[EventSink]
          + | None = None` to `run_scenario`. The UI worker passes a `Que
          +ueEventSink`; the main thread drains the queue and renders. Th
          +e `FileEventSink` (events.jsonl) still writes as before. Emiss
          +ion stays on the single driver thread, so the non-thread-safe 
          +`seq` counter is safe.                                        
      120  
      103 -**Structure Decision**: [Document the selected structure and r
          -eference the real                                             
      104 -directories captured above]                                   
      121 +3. **Transport: in-process thread + in-memory queue.** `run_co
          +ntroller.py` spawns a daemon thread running `run_scenario(...,
          + extra_sinks=[QueueEventSink(q)])`; the Streamlit main thread 
          +drains `q` in a loop, rendering events as they arrive, until a
          + `run_complete` event (or thread death). No subprocess, no dis
          +k polling for liveness. The chart frame is read **once** at co
          +mpletion from `forecast_comparison.csv` (run_scenario will als
          +o return its path). The worker never calls `st.*`.

      106 -## Complexity Tracking                                        
      123 +4. **Provider flip + fail-fast.** Rewrite `_detect_llm_provide
          +r()` to return `anthropic` if `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` set, else `b
          +edrock` if `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` set, else `raise ConfigError(..
          +.)` at resolve time (FR-029). The UI surfaces that `ConfigErro
          +r` as a clear pre-run message. Bedrock-form model ids (`us.ant
          +hropic.claude-opus-4-8`, `us.anthropic.claude-sonnet-4-6`) tra
          +nslate to native ids via the existing `_BEDROCK_TO_ANTHROPIC_M
          +ODEL_ID` table when provider is `anthropic`, so the UI always 
          +passes Bedrock-form ids and the backend resolves them.

          +1`. Extend it (and `run_scenario`'s custom-CSV branch) to acce
          +pt `train_ratio`, `val_ratio`, `test_ratio` (validated to sum 
          +to 1 within tolerance) so the UI's three inputs are honored. S
          +cenario runs are unaffected (they use metadata/golden split).

  The load-bearing decisions, distilled:
  1. Live agent streaming comes from switching the pipeline driver to
  app.stream() and emitting per super-step ‚ÄĒ keeping seq
  single-threaded/monotonic. The post-invoke reconstruction block is deleted to
  avoid double-emit. No edits to core/agent/engine.py or nodes.py.
  2. Transport = generic QueueEventSink + a backward-compatible extra_sinks
  param on run_scenario; UI worker thread runs the pipeline, main thread drains
  the queue. No subprocess, no disk polling for liveness.
  3. Provider flip to Anthropic-first / Bedrock-fallback with a fail-fast
  ConfigError; UI passes Bedrock-form model ids that translate automatically.
  4. Custom CSV gets a real three-fraction split (signature change), and the
  comparison frame is relabeled train/val/test for the chart.
  5. Cleanup is surgically scoped: delete streamlit_app.py, llm_reason.py,
  fallback.py (no external importers) and the embedded forecast HTML in
  drift/pipeline.py; keep the drift dataset-generation API (tests depend on it).

  the core touches, I'd suggest the task breakdown lead with the test-first

  .stream(), three-fraction split) before the UI build.

       81 +                                                              
       82 +def validate_split_fractions(train: float, val: float, test: f
          +loat) -> ValidationResult:                                    
       83 +    """The three fractions must sum to 1 within tolerance and 
          +each be positive (FR-009)."""                                 
       84 +    errors: list[str] = []                                    
       85 +    for name, frac in (("train", train), ("validation", val), 
          +("test", test)):                                              
       86 +        if frac is None or frac <= 0:                         
       87 +            errors.append(f"{name} fraction must be a positive
          + number (got {frac}).")                                       
       88 +    total = (train or 0) + (val or 0) + (test or 0)           
       89 +    if abs(total - 1.0) > _SPLIT_TOLERANCE:                   
       90 +        errors.append(f"train + validation + test must sum to 
          +1.0 (got {total:.4f}).")                                      
       91 +    return ValidationResult(ok=not errors, errors=errors)     
       92 +                                                              
       93 +                                                              
       94 +def validate_custom_series(                                   
       95 +    df: "pd.DataFrame | None",                                
       96 +    *,                                                        
       97 +    train: float,                                             
       98 +    val: float,                                               
       99 +    test: float,                                              
      100 +) -> ValidationResult:                                        
      101 +    """Full custom-CSV contract check, run BEFORE any pipeline
          + call (contract: custom_csv.md).                              
      102 +                                                              
      103 +    Covers: a DataFrame is present; columns are exactly ``ds``
          +/``y``; ``ds`` is datetime-parseable,                         
      104 +    chronologically sorted, and free of duplicate timestamps; 
          +``y`` is numeric and non-null; the                            
      105 +    split fractions sum to 1; and there are enough rows for ea
          +ch segment to hold >= 1 row.                                  
      106 +    """                                                       
      107 +    errors: list[str] = []                                    
      108 +                                                              
      109 +    if df is None:                                            
      110 +        return ValidationResult(ok=False, errors=["No CSV uplo
          +aded."])                                                      
      111 +                                                              
      112 +    # Columns must be exactly ds, y.                          
      113 +    cols = list(df.columns)                                   
      114 +    if cols[:2] != list(REQUIRED_CSV_COLUMNS) or len(cols) != 
          +2:                                                            
      115 +        errors.append(                                        
      116 +            "CSV must have exactly two columns named 'ds' (tim
          +e) and 'y' (value), in that order; "                          
      117 +            f"got {cols}."                                    
      118 +        )                                                     
      119 +        # Without the right columns the remaining checks are m
          +eaningless.                                                   
      120 +        return ValidationResult(ok=False, errors=errors)      
      121 +                                                              
      122 +    n = len(df)                                               
      123 +    if n == 0:                                                
      124 +        return ValidationResult(ok=False, errors=["CSV has no 
          +rows."])                                                      
      125 +                                                              
      126 +    # ds: datetime-parseable, sorted, unique.                 
      127 +    try:                                                      
      128 +        ds = pd.to_datetime(df["ds"])                         
      129 +    except (ValueError, TypeError):                           
      130 +        errors.append("Column 'ds' is not datetime-parseable."
          +)                                                             
      131 +        ds = None                                             
      132 +    if ds is not None:                                        
      133 +        if ds.duplicated().any():                             
      134 +            errors.append("Column 'ds' contains duplicate time
          +stamps.")                                                     
      135 +        if not ds.is_monotonic_increasing:                    
      136 +            errors.append("Column 'ds' must be sorted in chron
          +ological order.")                                             
      137 +                                                              
      138 +    # y: numeric, non-null.                                   
      139 +    y_numeric = pd.to_numeric(df["y"], errors="coerce")       
      140 +    if y_numeric.isna().any():                                
      141 +        errors.append("Column 'y' must be numeric with no miss
          +ing/empty values.")                                           
      142 +                                                              
      143 +    # Split fractions.                                        
      144 +    frac_result = validate_split_fractions(train, val, test)  
      145 +    errors.extend(frac_result.errors)                         
      146 +                                                              
      147 +    # Row-count feasibility (each segment >= 1 row after floor
          +ing, matching _series_split_from_df).                         
      148 +    if frac_result.ok:                                        
      149 +        test_rows = max(1, int(test * n))                     
      150 +        val_rows = max(1, int(val * n))                       
      151 +        train_rows = n - test_rows - val_rows                 
      152 +        if train_rows < 1:                                    
      153 +            errors.append(                                    
      154 +                f"Not enough rows ({n}) for this split ‚ÄĒ each 
          +of train/validation/test needs "                              
      155 +                "at least 1 row. Add more rows or adjust the f
          +ractions."                                                    
      156 +            )                                                 
      157 +                                                              
      158 +    return ValidationResult(ok=not errors, errors=errors)

      48 +    """Push ``event.to_dict()`` onto a stdlib queue for live in
         +-process consumption (FR-032).                                 
      49 +                                                               
      50 +    Used by the streamlined UI: the pipeline runs on a worker t
         +hread with this sink, and the

      52 +    raise ‚ÄĒ a raise would break ``EventEmitter.emit``'s sink fa
         +n-out loop and abort the run; a

      59 +    def write(self, event: StageEvent) -> None:                
      60 +        try:                                                   
      61 +            self._q.put_nowait(event.to_dict())                
      62 +        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 ‚ÄĒ never break the emi
         +t fan-out on a queue error

      144 +    override = ConfigOverride.from_dict(

      159 +        scenario_id = sel["scenario_id"]                      
      160 +    else:

      163 +            series_df=sel["custom_df"],                       
      164 +            train_ratio=sel["train_ratio"], val_ratio=sel["val
          +_ratio"], test_ratio=sel["test_ratio"],                       
      165 +            seasonal_period=int(sel["seasonal_period"]),      
      166 +            n_changepoints_to_detect=int(sel["n_changepoints_t
          +o_detect"]),                                                  
      167 +        )                                                     
      168 +                                                              
      169 +    try:                                                      
      170 +        handle = run_controller.start_run(scenario_id=scenario
          +_id, **kwargs)                                                
      171 +    except ConfigError as exc:                                
      172 +        st.error(f"Cannot start: {exc}")                      
      173 +        return                                                
      174 +                                                              
      175 +    st.subheader("Live event stream")                         
      176 +    stream_area = st.container()                              
      177 +    progress = st.empty()                                     
      178 +    rendered = 0                                              
      179 +    errored = False                                           
      180 +                                                              
      181 +    # Drain the queue on the main thread until run_complete, a
          +n error, or the worker dies.                                  
      182 +    while True:                                               
      183 +        events = run_controller.drain(handle, timeout=0.25)   
      184 +        for raw in events:                                    
      185 +            vm = event_view.from_event(raw)                   
      186 +            icon = "ūüõĎ" if vm.is_error else "‚ÄĘ"               
      187 +            with stream_area.expander(f"{icon} [{vm.seq}] {vm.
          +title} ‚ÄĒ {vm.summary}", expanded=vm.is_error):                
      188 +                if vm.payload_ref:                            
      189 +                    st.caption(f"(large payload offloaded to {
          +vm.payload_ref})")                                            
      190 +                st.json(vm.payload)                           
      191 +            rendered += 1                                     
      192 +            if vm.is_error:                                   
      193 +                errored = True                                
      194 +            if vm.stage == "run_complete":                    
      195 +                progress.empty()                              
      196 +                _render_results(handle)                       
      197 +                return                                        
      198 +        if errored:                                           
      199 +            progress.error("Run stopped due to an error (see t
          +he highlighted event above).")                                
      200 +            return

      202 +            break                                             
      203 +        progress.info(f"‚Ź≥ Agent working‚Ä¶ {rendered} events so
          + far.")                                                       
      204 +        time.sleep(0.05)                                      
      205 +                                                              
      206 +    # Worker finished without a run_complete event ‚Üí surface a
          +ny captured exception.                                        
      207 +    if handle.error is not None:                              
      208 +        progress.error(f"Run failed: {type(handle.error).__nam
          +e__}: {handle.error}")                                        
      209 +    elif handle.result is not None:                           
      210 +        progress.empty()                                      
      211 +        _render_results(handle)                               
      212 +                                                              
      213 +                                                              
      214 +def _render_results(handle: run_controller.RunHandle) -> None:
      215 +    result = handle.result                                    
      216 +    if not result:                                            
      217 +        return                                                
      218 +                                                              
      219 +    fe = result.get("final_eval")                             
      220 +    if fe:                                                    
      221 +        v = verdict_mod.derive(fe)                            
      222 +        (st.success if v.winner == "agent" else st.info)(f"ūüŹÜ 
          +{v.headline}")                                                
      223 +        c1, c2, c3 = st.columns(3)                            
      224 +        c1.metric("Agent MAE", f"{v.agent_mae:.3f}")          
      225 +        c2.metric("Full-history MAE", f"{v.full_history_mae:.3
          +f}")                                                          
      226 +        c3.metric("Naive MAE", f"{v.naive_mae:.3f}")          
      227 +                                                              
      228 +    csv_path = result.get("csv_path")                         
      229 +    if csv_path and Path(csv_path).exists():                  
      230 +        df = pd.read_csv(csv_path)                            
      231 +        changepoints = _changepoints_from_events(handle)      
      232 +        data = chart_mod.build_frame(df, changepoints=changepo
          +ints)                                                         
      233 +        st.plotly_chart(chart_mod.build_figure(data), use_cont
          +ainer_width=True)                                             
      234 +    else:                                                     
      235 +        st.warning("No comparison chart available for this run
          +.")                                                           
      236 +                                                              
      237 +                                                              
      238 +def _changepoints_from_events(handle: run_controller.RunHandle
          +) -> list[dict[str, Any]]:                                    
      239 +    """Best-effort: recover the detected-changepoints payload 
          +from the run_dir events.jsonl."""                             
      240 +    run_dir = (handle.result or {}).get("run_dir")            
      241 +    if not run_dir:                                           
      242 +        return []                                             
      243 +    path = Path(run_dir) / "events.jsonl"                     
      244 +    if not path.exists():                                     
      245 +        return []                                             
      246 +    import json                                               
      247 +                                                              
      248 +    for line in path.read_text().splitlines():                
      249 +        e = json.loads(line)                                  
      250 +        if e.get("stage") == "changepoint_detection" and e.get
          +("status") == "complete":                                     
      251 +            payload = e.get("payload", {})                    
      252 +            if isinstance(payload, dict):                     
      253 +                return payload.get("detected", [])            
      254 +    return []                                                 
      255 +

  front-end, thin over the changepoint agent:

  - Live streaming ‚ÄĒ switched the agent driver from app.invoke() to
  app.stream(stream_mode=["updates","values"]), emitting each in-graph stage as 
  its node completes and deleting the post-invoke reconstruction burst. Emission
  stays single-threaded ‚Üí seq monotonic, no double-emit.
  - QueueEventSink + extra_sinks param on run_scenario ‚ÄĒ in-process queue
  transport; the UI worker thread runs the pipeline, the main thread drains
  events live.
  - Provider flip ‚ÄĒ _detect_llm_provider() now prefers Anthropic API, falls back
  to Bedrock, and raises a clear ConfigError when neither is configured.
  - Three-fraction custom split + train/val/test region labels in
  forecast_comparison.csv + csv_path in the return dict.
  - T040 hardening ‚ÄĒ the Anthropic client is now built once per role, not per
  invoke.

  drift/fallback.py; stripped the embedded forecast HTML UI + /forecast/* +
  /changepoint/run from drift/pipeline.py ‚ÄĒ kept the dataset-generation API
  (test_api.py's 34 tests still green).

‚Źļ Good catches ‚ÄĒ let me address them. First the two clear fixes, then I'll dig
  into the diagnostics/tools for #3 (which needs a conversation about labels and
  grouping).

  On #1 (double events): Your screenshot confirms exactly what's happening. The
  prelude stages (changepoint detection, the two baselines, diagnostics) are
  emitted through the stage() context manager, which fires a start event (empty
  payload ‚Üí "0 detected", blank summary) and a complete event (filled payload ‚Üí
  "6 detected"). The UI is faithfully rendering both. config_resolved and
  split_built ([1],[2]) only appear once because they're emitted directly as
  complete. The clean fix is to render only complete/error events ‚ÄĒ each stage
  then appears once, when it finishes, still arriving live and in order.

  Let me apply #1 and #2.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  ūüďŹ History around changes (is there enough recent data?)
  | post_changepoint_history_len | History since last change | How many data
  points exist after the latest changepoint. |
  | post_changepoint_shorter_than_season | Too little history for a full season
  | True if the post-change history is shorter than one seasonal cycle (so
  seasonality may be unlearnable). |
  | seasonal_period | Seasonal period | The assumed length of one seasonal cycle
  (e.g. 365 for daily data). |

  ūüďä Segment & shift analysis (how big/permanent are the shifts?)
  | segment_stats | Segment statistics | Mean/spread of each stretch between
  changepoints. |
  | permanent_shift_magnitude | Permanent shift size | How far the latest
  segment's level sits from the first ‚ÄĒ a lasting level change. |
  | transient_event_score | Transient-vs-regime score | Whether the last shift
  looks like a temporary spike that reverted, vs a lasting regime change. |
  | local_boundary_jumps | Jumps at change boundaries | The size of the level
  jump right at each changepoint. |

  ūüóďÔłŹ Events & drift patterns (temporary blips, gradual drift, recurring calendar
  effects)
  | candidate_event_blocks | Candidate event blocks | Short windows that look
  like one-off events/outliers rather than regime changes. |
  | recurring_event_summary | Recurring calendar events | Whether events recur
  on a calendar pattern (e.g. same month each year). |
  | candidate_drift_intervals | Candidate drift intervals | Stretches where the
  level drifts gradually rather than jumping. |

  Tools (6) ‚ÄĒ proposed grouping

  ūü™ü Refocus on recent data
  | recent_window | Retrain on recent window | Drop older history and retrain
  only from a recent changepoint ‚ÄĒ good when the past no longer applies. |

  ūüß© Keep full history + targeted correction
  | full_history_step_regressor | Mark permanent level shifts | Keep all data,
  add step markers at changepoints to model permanent jumps. |
  | full_history_ramp_regressor | Model gradual drift | Keep all data, add ramps
  to capture gradual drift. |
  | full_history_clean_event | Clean out one-off events | Keep all data, smooth
  over temporary event blocks so they don't distort the fit. |
  | full_history_prophet_tuned_holidays | Tune recurring calendar events |
  Encode recurring events as holidays and tune the forecaster's sensitivity. |

  ūüõü Safe default
  | full_history_default (always on) | Default forecast (always on) | Plain
  forecast on all training history ‚ÄĒ the guaranteed-valid fallback; can't be
  turned off. |

‚Źļ All 129 targeted tests pass. All three changes are complete and verified.

  Summary

  1. Double events ‚ÄĒ fixed. The duplication was the start/complete pair each
  stage emits through the stage() context manager: the start showed an empty
  payload ("0 detected", blank summary) and the complete showed the real result
  ("6 detected"). The live-stream loop in app.py now skips start events and
  renders only the terminal complete/error event ‚ÄĒ so every stage appears
  exactly once, when it finishes, still live and in order.
  (config_resolved/split_built were never doubled because they emit directly as
  complete.)

  2. Legend repositioned ‚ÄĒ fixed. In chart.py the legend is now horizontal,
  anchored bottom-right and below the rangeslider/minimap (y=-0.32, 110px bottom
  margin), clearing the top of the plot entirely. The changepoint markers now
  use terse labels (CP őĒ=+0.20), alternate left/right to avoid overlapping each
  other, and have the top to themselves.

  3. Diagnostics & tools ‚ÄĒ labelled, grouped, and documented. All 13 diagnostics
  and 6 tools now show human-readable names with a native ? help tooltip on
  each checkbox, organized under bold umbrella sub-headers:
  - Diagnostics ‚Üí ūüďć Detected changes ¬∑ ūüďŹ History around changes ¬∑ ūüďä Segment &
  shift analysis ¬∑ ūüóďÔłŹ Events & drift patterns
  - Tools ‚Üí ūü™ü Refocus on recent data ¬∑ ūüß© Keep full history + targeted
  correction ¬∑ ūüõü Safe default (the always-on fallback, shown locked)

  Each section also gained a one-line caption ("what the agent is allowed to
  see" / "do"). The labels/help/grouping live in config_builder.py (importable,
  testable), and a new lockstep test guarantees every backend key is covered in
  exactly one group with non-empty text ‚ÄĒ so if the bundle ever changes, the
  test fails rather than silently dropping an item. The raw keys stay internal
  for the override and event stream, exactly as before.

‚ĚĮ Why does the numbers skip [Image #5]. Also the legend is not visible [Image   
  #6]                                                                           
  ‚éŅ ¬†[Image #5]
  ‚éŅ ¬†[Image #6]

‚Źļ Two real issues, both with clear causes:

  1. Skipping numbers ‚ÄĒ the [N] shown is the raw emitter seq, which increments
  on both the start and complete event of each stage. Since the UI (correctly)
  renders only the complete event, the displayed seq jumps (1, 2, then 4, 6, 8,
  10‚Ä¶). The numbers aren't actually missing ‚ÄĒ they're the start events we
  deliberately hide. The fix: display a contiguous render counter instead of the
  raw seq.

  2. Legend clipped ‚ÄĒ placing the legend below the plot (y=-0.32) pushes it into
  the bottom margin, but the figure's height/margin didn't reserve enough room,
  so it's cut off at the figure's bottom edge. The fix: pin an explicit figure
  height with a generous bottom margin and a thinner rangeslider so the legend
  has dedicated space.

  Let me fix #1 first.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚ĚĮ Now the graphs are not coming [Image #7] What is happening?                   
  ‚éŅ ¬†[Image #7]

‚Źļ The stream finished correctly ([11] winner: agent) but the verdict + chart
  didn't render. This is a race condition: when the UI sees the run_complete
  event in the queue, it immediately calls _render_results(handle) ‚ÄĒ but
  handle.result is set only after run_scenario returns, which happens a hair
  later than the event being emitted. So result is still None and nothing
  renders. Let me confirm by reading the relevant code.

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚Źļ Confirmed. Two compounding problems:

  1. Race: _render_results is called the instant the run_complete event arrives,
  but handle.result (set when run_scenario returns) may not be populated yet ‚Üí
  _render_results hits if not result: return and silently renders nothing.
  2. Even the fallback path (line¬†240) only renders if handle.result happens to
  be set by then ‚ÄĒ but after a return at line 228, it's never reached anyway.

  The fix: when run_complete arrives, wait for the worker thread to actually 
  finish (join it) so handle.result/handle.error are populated, then render. Let
  me fix this robustly.

‚Źļ All 37 UI tests pass.

  What was happening

  The stream completed correctly (you saw [11] Run complete ‚ÄĒ winner: agent),
  but the verdict + chart never rendered because of a race condition:

  - The backend emits the run_complete event just before run_scenario returns.
  - The UI saw that event in the queue and immediately called
  _render_results(handle) ‚ÄĒ but handle.result is only set when the worker
  thread's run_scenario call actually returns, a moment later.
  - So _render_results found handle.result is None, hit its if not result: 
  return, and silently rendered nothing.

  The fix

  When the run_complete event arrives, the UI now joins the worker thread first
  (handle.thread.join()) ‚ÄĒ guaranteeing run_scenario has returned and
  handle.result/handle.error are populated ‚ÄĒ then renders. It shows a brief "‚Ź≥
  Finalizing results‚Ä¶" while joining. I also made _render_results defensive: if
  results are ever genuinely missing it now surfaces the captured error or a
  clear warning instead of rendering blank.

  The end-to-end simulation confirms handle.result is populated after the join,
  the verdict derives, and the chart builds with all four traces. Reload and run
  again ‚ÄĒ the verdict banner, the three MAE metrics, and the interactive graph
  should now appear after the stream finishes.

‚Źļ The geometry is now provably safe. The math:

  - Figure 640px tall, with 40px top + 200px bottom margins ‚Üí 400px plot area.
  - Rangeslider takes ~7% of the plot (~28px) at the bottom of the plot area.
  - Legend top sits at ~492px from the figure top ‚ÄĒ that's ~52px below the
  plot's bottom axis (clear of the ~28px minimap) ‚ÄĒ leaving ~148px of clearance
  to the figure's bottom edge. Plenty of room for the legend row to render fully
  without clipping.

  The earlier versions clipped because a negative legend y is measured in
  plot-area fractions, not pixels ‚ÄĒ so y=-0.30 actually dropped the legend
  ~120px+ below the plot, past the figure edge. Now y=-0.13 (√ó400px = ~52px)
  keeps it comfortably inside the 200px bottom band.

  minimap with room to spare. If you'd like it even more separated from the
  minimap, nudging y from -0.13 toward -0.18 moves it lower while staying inside
  the 200px band.
